Looking at owned AIO keywords, TGG is performing well with 11,400 keywords and a notable 22.6% month-over-month increase, while HN, AO, and JB trail behind. AI visibility metrics from Profound show TGG leading at 17.8%, with HN, AO, and JB at 12.7%, 11.7%, and 8.3% respectively. I notice the AI citations data isn't in the spreadsheet—the markdown report shows TGG at 3.0% and AO at 3.2%, but there's no historical trend to compare. The CTR data table only goes through February 2026, so there's no updated March comparison available. I'm flagging a critical data discrepancy—the GA4 sheet shows blank LLM sessions for March, but Profound and the markdown report both indicate 25,800 sessions, so I need to determine which source is authoritative and whether GA4 data is actually missing or just not populated.

Looking at the historical pattern, GA4 and Profound have consistently shown significant differences—January had GA4 at 22,509 versus Profound at 34,600, and February showed 15,868 versus 25,200—so the March figure of 25,800 appears to align with Profound's methodology. The AI visibility metric shows a dramatic decline from 60.8% in January down to 19.4% in February and 17.8% in March, but the markdown report notes this reflects a methodology shift where they increased tracked prompts from around 400 to over 2,200, making the January trend incomparable to the later months. I need to be careful in the narrative to frame this as a data collection change rather than actual performance degradation. The citations data is also missing from the spreadsheet, so I'll need to flag that gap as well.

On the citations front, the March figures show AO at 3.2% has actually pulled ahead of TGG at 3.0%, which triggers the escalation flag mentioned in the skill guidelines. The non-branded metrics are deteriorating—year-over-year clicks worsened from -22.2% in February to -25.6% in March, and non-brand's share of total traffic dropped from 39.6% last March to 35.2% this March. Organic shopping keywords also declined month-over-month from 16,700 to 14,900, a 10.8% drop that contradicts the growth story we're trying to tell.

I'm noticing some data gaps that complicate the full picture: the CTR table only extends through February 2026, the Keywords in Top 3 metric that appeared in previous reports is missing from this month's MD report, and SERP Volatility data isn't available in either the spreadsheet or report. On the positive side, revenue is up 1.5% year-over-year despite sessions being down 5.7%, which reinforces the efficiency narrative.

The competitor AI visibility metrics are all declining month-over-month across the board—TGG, HN, AO, and JB—which suggests this might be a broader measurement or landscape shift rather than a TGG-specific issue. The MD report also flags that total citations to retailers dropped 8% month-over-month, adding context that the AI shopping environment itself is changing. **Active skills:** tgg-monthly-seo-report

## Data I have and can work with

**Organic performance (from xlsx):** Sessions 2.26M (+10.3% MoM, -5.7% YoY), Revenue $13.24M (+8.0% MoM, +1.5% YoY), Conv rate 1.2% (+8.0% YoY). Non-branded clicks 445K (-25.6% YoY, ~flat MoM). Non-branded impressions 17.8M (+8.4% YoY). Branded clicks 818K (-10.5% YoY).

**AI metrics (from xlsx + MD):** AI Visibility 17.8% (#1), Citations 3.0% (#2, AO leads at 3.2%). LLM sessions 25,800 (Profound, +2.4% MoM). LLM revenue $201K (+33.2% MoM). Owned AIO KWs 11,400 (+22.6% MoM). Total AIO KWs 14,300 (+5.1% MoM).

**Shopping (from xlsx):** Organic shopping KWs 14,900 (-10.8% MoM). GMC clicks 265K (flat MoM). GMC impressions 14M (-0.7% MoM). Shopping sessions 137K, revenue $752K.

**Focus & Outcomes table** from MD report.

## Issues to flag

**1. AO has overtaken TGG on AI Citations (3.2% vs 3.0%).** Your skill flags this as a red flag. The MD report notes TGG is #2 on citations. You need to decide how to frame this: acknowledge and explain, or bury it. I'd recommend acknowledging it, since AO was also ahead earlier (they led Sep-Nov 2025) and the gap is small. The overall citations market dropped 8% MoM industry-wide, so the real story is structural, not competitive.

**2. LLM Sessions source discrepancy.** GA4 data is blank for March in the xlsx. Profound shows 25,800. Feb GA4 was 15,868 but Profound was 25,200. These are materially different numbers (Profound runs ~60% higher). The MD report uses 25,800 (Profound). Jan report used GA4 at 22,509. You've switched sources between months without noting it. Which is canonical going forward? The Feb MD report said "25,200 MoM +2.38%" but the xlsx GA4 shows Feb at 15,868. Need to pick one and stick with it.

**3. AI Visibility trend is non-comparable pre/post Feb.** The jump from 60.8% (Jan) to 19.4% (Feb) to 17.8% (Mar) is a methodology change (prompt set expansion ~550%). You handled this in Feb but the Mar deck should not show the Sep-Jan numbers alongside Feb-Mar without making the break explicit. Otherwise stakeholders will think visibility cratered.

**4. Organic shopping KWs dropped -10.8% MoM** (16,700 → 14,900). This breaks the "growing footprint" narrative from prior months. JB collapsed even harder (14,800 → 10,300). Worth investigating if this is a Semrush measurement artefact or real. Did Google reduce shopping module appearances in March?

**5. CTR table has no March data.** Latest column is Feb 2026. If you want to continue the CTR compression story, you need March CTR data from OD or GSC.

**6. Keywords in Top 3 (non-brand) not in the data.** Jan was 31,729, Feb was 31,756. March number is missing from the xlsx and MD report. Do you have this from Semrush?

**7. Non-brand % of total clicks** dropped to 35.2% (from 39.6% in Mar-25, 36.5% in Feb-26). This is a meaningful structural shift worth reporting. Branded clicks are holding better than non-branded.

**8. Revenue YoY is +1.5%.** This is weaker than Feb's +12.7% YoY. Still positive, still the "doing more with less" story, but the margin is thin. Worth checking: is Mar-25 a tough comp? Yes, Mar-25 revenue was $13.04M, which was itself +24.6% YoY. So +1.5% on top of +24.6% is actually a strong two-year stack.

**9. Focus & Outcomes table.** Several rows look updated from Feb. I'd flag these for your review: "AI tracking foundation" moved to 🟢 (good, highlight this). "PDP FAQs V2" and "PDP AI rendering audit" are still ⚪. "AI Commerce Content" and "AI-optimised product descriptions" are new additions since Feb. Confirm all latest results are genuinely current.

## External context (cite as speculation)

**Google March 2026 core update** started March 27, completed April 8. The first core update of 2026, following a spam update and a Discover update. Google described it as a regular update to surface relevant, satisfying content. SE Ranking data showed nearly 80% of top-3 results shifted positions, higher volatility than December 2025. This means March data (1-31) mostly reflects the Feb volatility recovery, but the last 4 days of March had the new core update rolling. April data will show the real impact.

**March spam update** completed March 24-25 in under 20 hours, the fastest ever.

**AI Overviews on shopping queries** now at ~14% of all shopping queries, a 5.6x increase in just four months according to Visibility Labs.

**Google UCP updates (March 19)** added multi-item cart support, real-time product data, and identity linking for loyalty programmes. Simplified onboarding rolling out in Merchant Center. This is relevant context for the feed optimisation workstream.

## What I need from you before building slides

1. **LLM Sessions:** Which source is canonical, GA4 or Profound? And can you get the March GA4 figure?
2. **Keywords in Top 3/10/100 (non-brand):** March numbers from Semrush.
3. **March CTR data:** If you want to include it. Not essential every month.
4. **SERP Volatility score** for March (Semrush Sensor).
5. **Organic Revenue:** Confirm $13.24M is correct from GA4 (the xlsx has it).
6. **Confirm the AI Visibility table approach:** Show Sep-Jan old prompt set alongside Feb-Mar new prompt set with a clear break? Or just show Feb-Mar?
7. **Focus & Outcomes:** Confirm all rows are updated. Specifically flag any that are unchanged from Feb.

## Proposed narrative arc

March is a "recovery + structural pressure" month. The headline could be something like: **"March recovery confirms ranking resilience. Non-brand clicks continue structural decline as AI and shopping capture more of the SERP."**

The story: rankings bounced back from Feb volatility (+10.3% sessions MoM), revenue is positive YoY (+1.5% on a strong comp), and AI leadership holds (#1 visibility, 5.1pp lead). But non-branded clicks are down -25.6% YoY, worsening from Feb's -22.2%. The clicks that used to reach organic listings are being intercepted by AI Overviews, shopping carousels, and ads. TGG's response (feed optimisation, PDP content, AI visibility) is the right strategy. Two new core updates are now live (spam + core) with April impact still TBD.

This month doesn't need Feb's depth. Standard 5-6 slides plus focus & outcomes.

What data can you get me to fill the gaps?

The non-brand CTR is historically much higher because branded queries dilute position 1 performance, but interestingly the current non-brand CTR is now lower than the all-query CTR, which suggests something shifted in the composition or performance dynamics.

AI Overviews and shopping carousels are hitting non-brand queries harder than the blended data indicated. The March recovery is notable though—position 1 bounced from 9.17% to 14.86% month-over-month, a 62% jump that tracks with the ranking stabilization after February's volatility. ## Confirmed data inventory for March report

**Organic**
- Sessions: 2,260,622 (MoM +10.3%, YoY -5.7% on top of +2.4% in Mar-25)
- Revenue: $13,243,923 (MoM +8.0%, YoY +1.5% on top of +24.6% in Mar-25)
- Conv Rate: 1.20% (YoY +8.0%)
- Keywords in Top 3 (non-brand): 31,765 (MoM +9.5%, YoY +1.1%)
- Non-brand clicks: 445,030 (MoM -0.7%, YoY -25.6%)
- Non-brand impressions: 17.78M (MoM +9.1%, YoY +8.4%)

**AI Metrics (Profound canonical)**
- AI Visibility: 17.8% (#1). HN 12.7%, AO 11.7%, JB 8.3%
- AI Citations: 3.0% (#2). AO 3.2%, HN 1.4%, JB 0.8%
- LLM Sessions: 25,800 (MoM +2.4%)
- LLM Revenue: $201K (MoM +33.2%)
- Owned AIO KWs: 11,400 (MoM +22.6%)

**Shopping**
- GMC Clicks: 265,111 (flat MoM)
- Organic Shopping KWs: 14,900 (MoM -10.8%)
- Shopping Purchases: 4,306 (MoM -1.9%)
- Shopping Revenue: $751,614 (MoM -3.7%)

**CTR (non-brand, from CSV)**
- Pos 1: 14.86% (YoY -77.4%, MoM +62.1%)
- Pos 2: 11.66% (YoY -59.0%, MoM +27.2%)
- Pos 3: 12.73% (YoY -39.7%, MoM +39.0%)
- Pos 1-3 Avg YoY: -58.7%

---

## Issues and observations

**CTR data tells two stories.** The xlsx CTR table (which appears to be blended brand + non-brand) showed Feb pos 1 at 17.5% with -54% YoY. The CSV (non-brand only) shows March pos 1 at 14.86% with -77.4% YoY. Non-brand CTR compression is worse than the blended figure reported in February. However, the MoM recovery is strong (+62% pos 1). This aligns with ranking recovery. For March, I wouldn't go deep on CTR again (you covered that in Feb), but the non-brand figure is worth a footnote update, e.g. "Non-brand CTR for pos 1 recovered to 14.9% in March (from 9.2% in Feb) but remains -77% YoY."

**AO overtook on Citations (3.2% vs 3.0%).** This happened before (Sep-Nov 2025) and you recovered. The gap is 0.2pp, and the whole market dropped ~8% MoM. I'd frame it as: TGG maintains #1 visibility with a comfortable lead. Citations dipped to #2 as total AI citations to retailers declined industry-wide. The distinction between visibility (mentions) and citations (source links) matters here, and the visibility lead is the more durable metric.

**Organic Shopping KWs down -10.8%.** JB collapsed even harder (-36%, 14,800 → 10,300). HN also dropped. This looks like a Semrush measurement fluctuation or Google pulling back shopping modules in some categories during the update period. GMC clicks being dead flat supports this being a visibility measurement issue rather than a real traffic loss. Don't spin it as growth. Note it as a dip and watch next month.

**The xlsx you uploaded is identical to the project file.** No new data in it vs what we already had.

**Focus & Outcomes table (from MD report).** Comparing Feb → Mar:

| Row | Changed? | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| AI tracking foundation | Yes, moved to 🟢 | Highlight: Profound chosen, onboarding starting |
| SERP Changes: CTR | Yes | Updated with 54-67% decline finding, shifting to product work |
| Blog AI summaries | Yes | Content completed, in review, moving to dev bulk upload |
| AI-ready PLP intro copy | Yes | 1,059 done, writing remaining 843 |

## Issues and observations

**CTR data tells two stories.** The xlsx CTR table (which appears to be blended brand + non-brand) showed Feb pos 1 at 17.5% with -54% YoY. The CSV (non-brand only) shows March pos 1 at 14.86% with -77.4% YoY. Non-brand CTR compression is worse than the blended figure reported in February. However, the MoM recovery is strong (+62% pos 1). This aligns with ranking recovery. For March, I wouldn't go deep on CTR again (you covered that in Feb), but the non-brand figure is worth a footnote update, e.g. "Non-brand CTR for pos 1 recovered to 14.9% in March (from 9.2% in Feb) but remains -77% YoY."

**AO overtook on Citations (3.2% vs 3.0%).** This happened before (Sep-Nov 2025) and you recovered. The gap is 0.2pp, and the whole market dropped ~8% MoM. I'd frame it as: TGG maintains #1 visibility with a comfortable lead. Citations dipped to #2 as total AI citations to retailers declined industry-wide. The distinction between visibility (mentions) and citations (source links) matters here, and the visibility lead is the more durable metric.

**Organic Shopping KWs down -10.8%.** JB collapsed even harder (-36%, 14,800 → 10,300). HN also dropped. This looks like a Semrush measurement fluctuation or Google pulling back shopping modules in some categories during the update period. GMC clicks being dead flat supports this being a visibility measurement issue rather than a real traffic loss. Don't spin it as growth. Note it as a dip and watch next month.

**The xlsx you uploaded is identical to the project file.** No new data in it vs what we already had.

### SLIDE 1 — Overview KPIs
**Template source:** Feb slide 1 (keep layout exactly)

**Title:** `Monthly SEO Overview - March rankings recover, non-brand decline continues`

**Period line:** `Period: March 2026 | Compared to: MoM & YoY | Migration: Jul-25`

**4 KPI tiles:**

| Tile | Value | MoM % | YoY % |
|---|---|---|---|
| Organic Sessions | 2,260,622 | +10.34 | -5.74 |
| Organic Revenue | $13,243,923 | +8.0 | +1.53 |
| Keywords in Top 3 (Non-brand) | 31,765 | +9.5 | +1.1 |
| AI Visibility Score | 17.8% (Rank #1) | -1.6pp | N/A |

**Organic sessions table:** Update the 2026 column. Jan: 2,633,232. Feb: 2,048,865. Mar: 2,260,622 (highlight yellow). Apr-Dec: dash.

**YoY 26v25 column:** Jan: -1.27%. Feb: -4.56%. Mar: -5.74%.

**4 bullet points (right column):**

1. **Organic Sessions recovered +10.3% MoM** to 2.26M as Google rolled back February algorithm volatility. Rankings began stabilising from ~March 14. YoY -5.74% reflects structural CTR compression, not a ranking issue. Non-brand CTR for position 1 at 14.9%, down 77% YoY (updated to non-brand only view).

2. **Organic Revenue +1.53% YoY** to $13.24M on top of a strong +24.6% YoY Mar-25 comp. Conversion rate 1.20%, up 8% YoY. Keywords in Top 3 up +9.5% MoM and +1.1% YoY.

3. **Non-branded clicks -25.6% YoY** (445K), worsening from Feb's -22.2%. Non-brand impressions grew +8.4% YoY to 17.8M, confirming CTR compression is the driver, not reduced search demand.

4. **AI Visibility #1 among retail competitors at 17.8%**, #4 overall (behind Samsung, Breville, LG). 5.1pp ahead of HN (12.7%). Citations 3.0% (#2, AO leads at 3.2%). LLM sessions 25.8K, $201K revenue.

**Competitor mini-table (bottom-right):**

| Mar-26 | AI Visibility | AI Citation Rate |
|---|---|---|
| **The Good Guys** | **17.8%** | **3.0%** |
| Harvey Norman | 12.7% | 1.4% |
| Appliances Online | 11.7% | 3.2% |
| JB Hi-Fi | 8.3% | 0.8% |

**Blue box footnote:** Replace Samsung/choice.com.au text with: `"TGG is #1 among direct retail competitors and #4 overall in AI visibility (behind Samsung, Breville, LG). TGG holds #1 in visibility among retail competitors every month since tracking began (Sep 2025)."`

**Bottom footnotes:** Keep existing definitions. Update AI Visibility Score line to add: `"Note: Score reflects Profound onboarded prompt set (~2,200 prompts). Drop from Jan 60.8% is a methodology change on full platform onboarding, not a real decline."`
